## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / ecological growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by current population size P and possibly explicit time forcing t, which is the standard setup for continuous-time ecological population dynamics. Typical relationships encode per-capita growth, density dependence (crowding), Allee effects at low density, harvesting, and seasonal/environmental forcing via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Time-trend in intrinsic growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradual environmental change affecting per-capita growth)
- Seasonally forced per-capita growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment/resources)
- Gompertz growth (log-density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines with log of population size)
- Theta-logistic / power density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**(c2 + 1) (crowding effects stronger/weaker than quadratic depending on c2)
- Richards-type generalized crowding via reciprocal carrying scale: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible approach to saturation with shape exponent)
- Allee effect with crowding limitation (strong Allee): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth below threshold c1; saturation via c2)
- Weak Allee factor (saturating at low P): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (P / (P + c2)) (reduced growth at low density without strict threshold)
- Constant-yield harvesting/removal: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 (fixed removals independent of P, e.g., quota harvest)
- Proportional harvesting/removal: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (net per-capita growth reduced by exploitation)
- Stocking/immigration plus density effects: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 + c2 (constant input term modeling immigration/stocking)
- Additive seasonal forcing (resource-driven pulses): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (seasonal net influx/outflux independent of P)
- Catastrophic mortality pulse (localized in time): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * exp(-c2 * (t - c3)**2) * P (episodic event causing temporary extra mortality)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth structure: if dP_dt / P is approximately constant, models of the form dP_dt = f(t) * P are favored (density-independent growth with time-varying rate).
- Crowding/competition: if dP_dt / P decreases with P, include negative density-dependent terms like -c * P**m (m>1) or log-based decline via P*log(c/P).
- Saturation via reciprocal scale: carrying-capacity-like limits often appear as factors (1 - c * P) or (1 - (c * P)**m), where c acts like 1/K.
- Allee effects at low density: if growth is suppressed at small P, include factors like (P - c) or P/(P + c) multiplying the growth term.
- Harvesting/exploitation signatures: constant offsets (-c) indicate quota-like removals; proportional terms (-c * P) indicate effort proportional to abundance.
- External inputs: additive +c or +c*sin(Ï‰ t) suggest immigration/stocking or seasonal recruitment not directly proportional to current P.
- Seasonality: periodic patterns in residuals vs t suggest embedding sin(c*t+c) in coefficients multiplying P or as additive forcing.
- Shock events: abrupt temporary deviations in growth vs t motivate localized pulses such as exp(-c*(t-c)**2) multiplying P (event-driven mortality/reduction).

`PÂ²/(aP+b)` is rational. `P*log(1+c4/P)` is not rational (it has a Taylor expansion `c4 - c4Â²/(2P) + ...` for large P, but this is an infinite series). These are fundamentally different function types. No match possible without setting c3=0, but then we'd just have `Pc0 + c5 + Pc1*exp(c2*t)` which is `P*(c0) + c5 + P*c1*exp(c2*t)`. This can't produce `PÂ²/(aP+b)`.

Candidate 43 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 44:** `Pc0 + Pc1*exp(c2*t) + Pc3/(Pc4+c5) + c6/(Pc4+c5)`

`Pc0 + [Pc3+c6]/(Pc4+c5)` over common denominator: `[Pc0*(Pc4+c5) + Pc3+c6]/(Pc4+c5)` = `[c0c4*PÂ² + (c0c5+c3)*P + c6]/(Pc4+c5)`.

Candidate 44 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 45:** `Pc0 + Pc1*exp(c2*t) + Pc3*log(c4/(P+c5)+1)`

`Pc3*log(c4/(P+c5)+1)` is transcendental in P. Can `Pc0 + Pc3*log(c4/(P+c5)+1)` = `PÂ²/(aP+b)`?

No â€” log is transcendental, rational functions are algebraic. They can't be equal for all P. Setting c3=0 leaves only `Pc0 + Pc1*exp(c2*t)` which can't produce the rational PÂ² term.

Candidate 45 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 46:** `Pc0 + Pc1*exp(c2*t) + Pc3/(Pc4+c5) + c6 + c7/(Pc4+c5)`

**Candidate 48:** `PÂ²c0/(P+c1) + Pc2*exp(c3*t)`

Over `(P+c1)`: `[PÂ²c0 + Pc2*exp*(P+c1)]/(P+c1)` = `[PÂ²c0 + PÂ²c2*exp + Pc1c2*exp]/(P+c1)`.

This matches GT form! The ratio of P*exp coefficient to PÂ²*exp coefficient is fixed at c1. In GT, the ratio is c5/c4 (from the denominator constants). Since c1 here IS the denominator constant, this is consistent.

Let me verify: GT = `[A*PÂ² + B*PÂ²*exp(ct) + C*P*exp(ct)]/(D*P+E)` where C/B = E/D (= c5/c4 in GT = 1/9.871 â‰ˆ 0.1013).

The overall constant adjusts. This works!

Candidate 48 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 49:** `Pc0 + Pc1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4*cos(c5*t+c6) + c7*Max(0,P+c8)`
